| OBS-064-T2-250 | OBSERVATION | Eph 1:7 | Yes — forgiveness is structurally linked to suffering. The atoning mechanism (Eph 1:7 — "through his blood"; Heb 9:22 — "without the shedding of blood there is no forgiveness") grounds forgiveness in suffering on the forgiver's side. The somatic compassion (splagchnizomai — Mat 18:27) is a suffered response in the forgiver's body. OBS-064-022, OBS-064-028. |
| OBS-064-T2-251 | OBSERVATION | Eph 1:7 | Suffering is the cost-side of forgiveness on the forgiver's part. The divine cost is the highest: the death of Christ (Eph 1:7). The human cost is the absorbed wrong: the forgiver absorbs the cost of the offence rather than extracting it. Suffering does not produce forgiveness mechanically but is structurally necessary to it — the release of the claim always involves the claim-holder absorbing what was owed. OBS-064-022, OBS-064-028. |
| OBS-099-T2-001 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | The evidence reveals that kindness (chesed) is God's defining relational attribute — not one quality among many but the one he most characteristically names when he identifies himself. Exo 34:6 establishes the canonical self-disclosure: God is "merciful and gracious, slow to anger, and abounding in steadfast love and faithfulness." The superlative grammar ("abounding") signals that chesed is characteristic of him in excess [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-089]. Lam 3:22 further establishes that God's chesed "never ceases" — permanence and inexhaustibility are definitional [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-085]. In the NT, chrēstotēs (G5544) is attributed directly to God in Rom 2:4 and Rom 11:22, where divine kindness is paired with severity as two expressions of the same covenantal faithfulness [XREG: G5544, OBS-099-091]. The character of God revealed: one whose inner disposition toward the creature is constitutively kind — stable, inexhaustible, and covenantally faithful. |
| OBS-099-T2-002 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Scripture explicitly and extensively attributes kindness to God in three forms: (a) direct predication — "God is kind to the ungrateful and evil" (Luke 6:35); "the Lord is kind in all his works" (Psa 145:17 [XREG: H2623, OBS-099-095]); (b) superlative attribution — "abounding in steadfast love" (Exo 34:6), "steadfast love is better than life" (Psa 63:3 [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-084]); (c) instrumental attribution — "God's kindness is meant to lead you to repentance" (Rom 2:4, OBS-099-076). The significance for the human person: divine kindness is God's defining attribute; the call for human kindness is ontological grounding — to be kind is to be what the image-bearer was created to be. The absence of kindness is not merely behavioural failure but dimming of the image. |
| OBS-099-T2-005 | OBSERVATION | Eph 2:7, Rom 2:4 | Yes. Eph 2:7 places divine kindness in an eschatological frame: "in the coming ages he might show the immeasurable riches of his grace in kindness toward us in Christ Jesus" [XREG: G5544, OBS-099-093]. Rom 2:4 establishes that divine kindness is purposively aimed at repentance — directed toward a future state not yet present [OBS-099-076]. Kindness has an eschatological trajectory: both in the recipient (transformation) and in the divine economy (immeasurable future display). |
| OBS-099-T2-009 | OBSERVATION | Eph 2:7 | Yes — three typological movements: (a) Covenantal: each individual divine chesed act participates in and points toward the one covenantal faithfulness underlying them all [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-089]. (b) Christological: Eph 2:7 names Christ as the supreme display of divine kindness — the eschatological revelation of what chesed has always been pointing toward [XREG: G5544, OBS-099-093]. (c) Human-divine mirror: Ruth's kindness, 1Sa 20:14, 2Sa 10:2 — each human chesed act is typological of the divine pattern [OBS-099-086, OBS-099-070/071]. |
| OBS-099-T2-016 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Working description: Kindness is a stable inner disposition of loyal goodwill toward another, rooted in the heart, that orients the whole person toward the practical benefit and relational flourishing of its object, regardless of desert. Constituted by faithfulness (holds across time and through failure), compassion (feels with the other), and absence of self-serving motivation. In divine form: inexhaustible, unconditional in ultimate terms, purposively aimed at transformation. In human form: creaturely, finite, Spirit-formed, called to mirror the divine pattern. Primary constitutional location: heart. Primary expression: deliberate relational action. Counterfeit: pleasant speech covering self-serving motivation (chrēstologia). |
| OBS-099-T2-021 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Yes — three contextual variations: (a) Divine vs. human scope: God's chesed inexhaustible; human chesed creaturely and can be withdrawn [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-083, Q&A-008]. (b) Comfort vs. affliction: Job 6:4 (afflicting presence) vs. Psa 23:4 (comforting presence) — same term, different mode by context and divine purpose [OBS-099-067/066]. (c) Purposive vs. sustaining: Rom 2:4 — kindness aimed at repentance; Luke 6:35 — kindness to ungrateful without stated aim [OBS-099-076, OBS-099-078]. Purposive dimension present in some contexts; absent as explicit feature in others. |
| OBS-099-T2-025 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Three sustained effects: (a) Moral formation into chesed-character — the chasid is the outcome of a life shaped by chesed [XREG: H2623, OBS-099-094]. (b) Repentance and transformation — Rom 2:4 names repentance as the sustained purpose of received divine kindness [OBS-099-076]. (c) Hope in desolation — Lam 3:22–23 — sustained knowledge of God's unfailing chesed produces groundedness that does not depend on circumstances [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-085]. |
| OBS-099-T2-029 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Three blocking conditions: (a) Pride and self-sufficiency — Jer 17:5 — trusting in man closes the person to divine chesed [OBS-099-047]. (c) Hardness of heart — Exo 7:14 — Pharaoh's hardened heart refuses the relational movement that divine kindness invites [OBS-099-059]. Hardness is the inner condition most directly opposed to receiving kindness. |
| OBS-099-T2-030 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Three modes evidenced: (a) Pharaoh — hardens further; non-reception intensifies inner rigidity [OBS-099-059]. | OBS-099-T2-047 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Yes — two modes: (a) As prerequisite: Hos 6:6 pairs chesed with "knowledge of God" — genuine kindness requires cognitive grasp of who God is [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-088]. (b) As denied: Rom 2:4 — failure of cognition preconditions presumption: "not knowing that God's kindness is meant to lead you to repentance" [OBS-099-076]. Kindness requires knowing God to flow genuinely, and knowing God's intention to be received correctly. |
| OBS-099-T2-052 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Yes — structurally. (a) Gen 44:32 — Judah's surety burden anticipates guilt if he fails [OBS-099-063]. Inner cost of loving-kindness (bearing responsibility for another) is conscience-engaging. (b) Hos 6:6 — ritual without chesed produces a bad conscience in the theological sense: worship while withholding what God desires [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-088]. (c) Rom 2:4 — "not knowing" = moral cognitive failure that a properly functioning conscience should catch [OBS-099-076]. Kindness engages conscience as the inner witness monitoring whether one's orientation is aligned with what one knows to be right. |
| OBS-099-T2-060 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Yes — both modes. (a) Change of orientation: Rom 2:4 — aimed at repentance (metanoia — change of mind/direction) [OBS-099-076]. Hos 6:6 (withdrawal of chesed as communal failure) and Mic 7:2 (godly has perished) suggest communal formation can be lost — individual reversibility not directly addressed. |
| OBS-099-T2-061 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Partial sequence visible in Rom 2:4: (a) encounter with divine kindness → (b) recognition of its purpose → (c) repentance (reorientation). Before-during-after structure for received divine kindness [OBS-099-076, Q&A-072]. Chasid formation arc implies longer sequence (encounter → formation → stable identity → eschatological preservation [XREG: H2623, OBS-099-094/095]) but individual steps are not explicitly sequenced in a single passage. |
| OBS-099-T2-065 | OBSERVATION | Eph 2:7, Rom 2:4 | Yes — three eschatological markers: (a) Eschatological escalation: Eph 2:7 — "in the coming ages he might show the immeasurable riches of his grace in kindness toward us in Christ Jesus" [XREG: G5544, OBS-099-093]. | OBS-099-T2-067 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Two partial sequences: (a) Eph 4:32 cluster — kindness → tenderheartedness → forgiveness [OBS-099-077, SP-099-009]. (b) Rom 2:4 — encounter with divine kindness → recognition → repentance — explicitly sequential [OBS-099-076, Q&A-072]. Kindness precedes repentance; it is the mechanism leading to it. | OBS-099-T2-068 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Three explicit causal relationships: (a) Divine kindness → repentance: Rom 2:4 — kindness is the causal agent aimed at producing repentance [OBS-099-076]. (b) Experienced divine kindness → praise: Psa 63:3 — chesed causes the praise response [XREG: H2617A, OBS-099-084]. (c) Received human kindness → mirrored kindness: 2Sa 10:2 — "as his father dealt loyally with me, so I will deal loyally with Hanun" — received kindness causes its reproduction [OBS-099-071]. Causal network: divine kindness → praise + repentance in recipient → motivates mirrored human kindness → sustains covenant relationships. |
| OBS-099-T2-070 | OBSERVATION | Eph 2:7 | Partial evidence for three boundaries: (a) Kindness vs. love: 1Cor 13:4 — kindness is a mode of love's operation, not its definition [OBS-099-072, Q&A-021]. Love is broader; kindness is the specific outward-oriented gracious-action mode. (b) Kindness vs. compassion: Eph 4:32 — kindness and tenderheartedness are distinct qualities [OBS-099-077]. Compassion feels; kindness acts from that feeling. (c) Kindness vs. grace: Eph 2:7 — grace names the favour; kindness names the disposition in which the favour is given [XREG: G5544, OBS-099-093]. Gap: boundaries implied by co-occurrence and context but not explicitly theorised. Session D needed for full boundary analysis. |
| OBS-099-T2-077 | OBSERVATION | Rom 2:4 | Although the mind is not explicitly named as kindness's constitutional location, the verse evidence shows kindness engaging the mind's cognitive-discernment function in two specific ways. First, Hos 6:6 — "I desire steadfast love and not sacrifice, the knowledge of God rather than burnt offerings" — pairs chesed with knowledge of God (da'at Elohim). Genuine chesed requires a cognitive grasp of who God is; without this knowledge, the person substitutes ritual for the real inner disposition. The mind's function of knowing and discerning is therefore prerequisite to genuine kindness [OBS-099-088]. Second, Rom 2:4 — "not knowing that God's kindness is meant to lead you to repentance" — names cognitive failure as the mechanism by which received kindness is misappropriated. A correctly functioning cognitive faculty recognises the purpose of divine kindness; a failing one presumes on it [OBS-099-076]. What this reveals: kindness is not a mind-level characteristic but it requires the mind's knowing-function to operate correctly — it is cognitively dependent without being cognitively located. |

**SD pointers — direct (0)**

(none)

### H6238 a.shar — to enrich (`mti_id=7585`)

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H6238` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: —
2. Registry: R215 wealth · Legacy C-cluster: unassigned
3. Sub-group: `M46-A` (Inner closure) · `M46-C` (The ordering of character and wealth) · `M46-D` (The inner life beyond material circumstance)
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 17
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=7585` · `md_version=3` · `vc_status=vc_completed`

**Meaning text**

1) to be or become rich or wealthy, enrich, pretend to be rich

1a) (Qal) to be or become rich

1b) (Hiphil)

1b1) to make rich

1b2) to gain riches

1c) (Hithpael) to enrich oneself, pretend to be rich

**Verses:** 17 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (3)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 3720 | 7585-001 | Term names the inner drive to become rich as the source of moral failure and self-deception — Ephraim declares 'I am rich; I have found wealth for myself; they cannot find iniquity in me' (Hos 12:8): the self-declaration of wealth as the ground of self-assessed innocence; corrupt shepherds thank God for their enrichment while exploiting the flock (Zec 11:5); hastening to be rich brings punishment (Pro 28:20); the wicked will not become rich (Job 15:29). The inner motivation to accumulate — when it is self-directed and operates through exploitation or self-deception — produces the inner-closure pattern of M46-A. Anchor: Hos 12:8. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-A — New VCG. M46-A. |
| 3721 | 7585-002 | Term names enrichment as the fruit of diligence and divine blessing — the hand of the diligent makes rich (Pro 10:4); the blessing of the Lord makes rich, and he adds no sorrow with it (Pro 10:22); the Lord makes poor and makes rich, brings low and exalts (1Sa 2:7). Inner character (diligence) produces material enrichment; divine blessing produces material enrichment without the hidden cost that self-generated accumulation carries. The same verb names enrichment as earned through character and as given through divine sovereignty. Anchor: Pro 10:22. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-C — New VCG. M46-C. |
| 3722 | 7585-003 | Term names the deliberate refusal of enrichment as an act of inner integrity and wisdom — Abram refuses to take a thread or sandal strap from the king of Sodom lest the king claim to have made him rich (Gen 14:23): the inner act of not-being-enriched to preserve the testimony of dependence on God alone; wisdom counsels do not toil to acquire wealth, be discerning enough to desist (Pro 23:4). The inner discipline of restraining the wealth-seeking drive is itself an inner-being act of ordering the inner life beyond material circumstance. Anchor: Gen 14:23. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-D — New VCG. M46-D. |

to be rich; (pf.) to have acquired wealth

to be, or become rich, acquire wealth Lk. 1:25; 1Tim. 6:9; troponym Lk. 12:21; metaphorically to abound in, be abundantly furnished with, 1Tim. 6:18; to be spiritually enriched, 2Cor. 8:9

<a id="t-H7600"></a>
### H7600 sha.a.nan — secure (`mti_id=413`)

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H7600` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R117 peace · Legacy C-cluster: C17
3. Sub-group: `M46-A` (Inner closure) · `M46-D` (The inner life beyond material circumstance)
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 10
5. Patch-authoring refs: `mti_id=413` · `md_version=3` · `vc_status=vc_completed`

**Verses:** 10 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (2)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1861 | 413-001 | Term names the inner condition of complacent ease that wealth and security produce — the settled, untroubled self-assurance of those whose material and social position has made them feel unthreatened. This ease is not the shalom of God's gift but a self-generated security that produces contempt for those in misfortune, blindness to coming judgment, and arrogance toward God. In Job 12:5 it produces contempt; in Amos 6:1 it receives a prophetic woe; in 2Ki 19:28 it is the inner ground of Assyrian rage against God. Anchor: Amo 6:1. |  |
| 1862 | 413-002 | Term names the divinely-given condition of secure quietness — the ease of God's people living in genuine peace and safety as the fruit of shalom, in contrast to the self-generated complacency of 413-001. The same inner phenomenology (settled, untroubled, at ease) has an entirely different ground: when God gives it, it is the condition of the redeemed community at rest. Anchor: Isa 32:18. |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (8)**

| Finding ID | Type | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-117-T2-016 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 48:22, Deu 29:19, Amo 6:1, Isa 26:3 | The negative definition is richly evidenced: (1) Peace is not the absence of war alone — the shalom vocabulary covers inner states that have nothing to do with military conflict (Isa 26:3, Psa 4:8, Lam 3:17); (2) Peace is not self-generated security — the false shalom pattern (2509-002, Deu 29:19) shows that self-claimed peace without covenant ground is its precise corruption; (3) Peace is not available to the wicked — Isa 48:22, 57:21 ("there is no peace for the wicked"); the moral character of the person determines whether shalom is accessible; (4) Peace is not silence or passivity — the silence vocabulary (H2790B, H2814, G4623) is distinct from shalom; silence is a condition that enables or expresses peace but is not peace itself; (5) Peace is not complacent ease — sha'anan (H7600 group 413-001) names self-generated ease as a vice (Amo 6:1: "woe to those who are at ease in Zion"), demonstrating that ease without divine ground is not shalom. The negative boundary: peace is not a condition the person achieves by themselves, claims without God's ground, or inhabits while in moral disorder. |
| OBS-117-T2-017 | OBSERVATION | Isa 26:3, Psa 4:8, Isa 32:17 | Peace vs. rest (nuach, menuchah): rest is the condition of cessation from striving, the physical and inner stopping; peace is the positive condition of wholeness that rest may produce or accompany. The two overlap heavily (nuach and shalom co-occur throughout the corpus) but are distinguishable: nuach can be refused by God as judgment (Deu 28:65 — no resting-place); shalom may persist even in movement and striving. Peace vs. joy (H7600/G1515 vs. R97): joy is the positive emotional response; peace is the positive existential condition that may produce joy but is distinct from it. Psa 35:27 (the Lord delights in welfare of his servant) — joy is the emotional response to shalom-welfare, not the same thing. Peace vs. trust (R163): trust is the inner act of reliance on God; peace is the inner condition that trust produces (Isa 26:3 — he trusts in you → perfect peace; Psa 4:8 — you alone make me dwell in safety → I lie down in peace). Trust precedes peace; peace is trust's outcome. Gap: the boundary between peace and righteousness (tsedaqah) is particularly important but incompletely addressed in Stage 2a — Isa 32:17 ("the effect of righteousness will be peace") makes peace the fruit of righteousness, but whether they are distinct or overlapping characteristics requires Session D analysis. |
| OBS-117-T2-018 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Jer 6:14, Deu 29:19, Psa 28:3 | Yes — and this is among the most analytically significant features of the peace registry. The false-peace pattern (2508-003 and 2509-002) shows that shalom is precisely the characteristic that can be falsely claimed: (1) False prophecy of shalom: Jer 6:14, 8:11, Eze 13:10, 13:16, Mic 3:5 — prophets cry "Peace, peace" when there is no peace (prior session, incorporated as source material); (2) Self-deceptive shalom: Deu 29:19 (2509-002, OBS-117-150) — "I shall be safe, though I walk in the stubbornness of my heart"; (3) Complacent ease (sha'anan, H7600 group 413-001) — the comfortable feel of worldly security mistaken for shalom; (4) Speaking shalom with evil in the heart: Psa 28:3, Jer 9:8 — "speaks peace to his neighbor while evil is in his heart." The implication: shalom is the most counterfeitable of inner-being characteristics because its absence-of-distress phenomenology can be replicated by complacency, self-deception, or false prophecy. Authentic shalom requires its proper ground (God, covenant, trust) while false shalom is the same phenomenological condition without that ground. |
| OBS-117-T2-020 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 30:15, 1Pe 3:4, Isa 32:18 | The data shows a rich cognate field. Hebrew near-synonyms functioning alongside shalom: (1) Nuach/menuchah (rest, resting-place) — the cessation-dimension of peace; (2) Nachat (H5183A — quietness) — the inner stillness dimension, co-occurs with shaqat in Isa 30:15 at the analytical summit; (3) Shaqat (H8252 — quiet/quieted) — the active quieting, most prominent in its paired form "quietness and trust" (Isa 30:15); (4) Sha'anan (H7600 — at ease) — the ease dimension, positively (Isa 32:18) and negatively (Amo 6:1); (5) Demamah (H1827 — profound silence) — the threshold silence before divine speech. Greek near-synonyms: eirēnē (G1515) is not a synonym but the translation equivalent; hēsuchia/hēsuchios (G2271/G2272) — quietness, the NT equivalent of the Hebrew silence vocabulary (1Pe 3:4 — gentle and quiet spirit); anesis (G0425) — relief/rest from pressure. The cognate field reveals that peace has an inner-face (the silence/stillness vocabulary) and an outer-face (the welfare/wholeness vocabulary), and shalom is the integrative term that spans both. |
| OBS-117-T2-022 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 53:5, Isa 38:17, Amo 6:1, Isa 32:18 | Yes — three paradoxes are documented: (1) Peace through suffering: Isa 53:5 ("the chastisement that brought us peace, and with his wounds we are healed") — peace is purchased through suffering, not despite it (OBS-117-147). The mechanism of peace is its opposite (pain, punishment); (2) Peace through bitterness: Isa 38:17 ("it was for my welfare [shalom] that I had great bitterness") — Hezekiah's retrospective: his suffering was the path to his welfare. The paradox: shalom-welfare arrived via its experiential opposite; (3) Complacent ease as false peace: H7600 group 413-001 (Amo 6:1) and group 413-002 (Isa 32:18) — the same experiential condition of ease is either vice (self-generated) or blessing (divinely given). Peace and its counterfeit may be phenomenologically indistinguishable. The paradoxes converge on a single insight: authentic shalom is not produced by the absence of suffering or difficulty but by the presence of the peace-giver. Its opposite conditions (suffering, bitterness, difficulty) can be the means by which it arrives. |
| OBS-117-T2-074 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Dan 10:19, Isa 32:17, Deu 28:65 | Peace enables agency — the peaceful person is constitutionally equipped to act in the world from a stable inner base rather than from reactive anxiety. Evidence: (1) Dan 10:19 — "peace be with you; be strong and of good courage" — the angelic peace-gift produces strength and courage for action; peace precedes and enables Daniel's capacity to act on the vision; (2) Isa 32:17 — "the effect of righteousness will be peace, and the result of righteousness, quietness and trust forever" — the peace condition produces trust, which is the basis for courageous action; (3) Deu 28:65 reverse — the absence of peace produces the "trembling heart" and "languishing soul" that impair agency; fearful and anxious people cannot act decisively. Conversely: complacent ease (H7600 group 413-001) impairs agency by producing false security and contempt for consequences — a corrupted form of "peace" that disengages agency. |
| OBS-117-T2-075 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Jam 3:18, Amo 6:1, Dan 10:19 | The agency pattern reveals that authentic peace is not passive or quietist but enables robust, courageous action in the world. The peaceful person is not inactive — Mordecai seeks welfare, the peacemakers sow righteousness, Christ makes peace through the cross. The silence/stillness vocabulary names the inner orientation that enables agency, not the absence of agency. The contrast with complacent ease (H7600 413-001) is decisive: the person who is "at ease in Zion" (Amo 6:1) is precisely the person who does not act when they should — complacency impairs agency. Authentic shalom liberates agency; false peace suppresses it. |
| OBS-117-T2-083 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Mal 2:6, Amo 6:1 | Authentic peace deepens conscientiousness; false peace impairs it. (1) Deepens: the person who is genuinely at peace is in a stable inner condition from which conscientious action flows — Mal 2:6 (walked in peace → turned many from iniquity); the stable inner orientation of peace produces consistent moral response; (2) Impairs: complacent ease (H7600 group 413-001, Amo 6:1 — "woe to those at ease in Zion") represents peace's corruption as conscientiousness-impairment — the at-ease person fails to respond to what conscience and moral awareness demand; false shalom produces precisely the opposite of conscientiousness: comfort without response. The distinction between authentic shalom and complacent ease is most sharply felt here: one deepens conscientiousness, the other destroys it. |

This directly answers the potential misunderstanding that peace means passivity or disengagement — the data establishes the opposite. Peace is the enabling condition for the most integrated form of moral-volitional-active response. |

### H8082 sha.men — rich (`mti_id=4695`)

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H8082` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R006 anointing · Legacy C-cluster: C16

## §4. Appendix — items linked at registry or collection level

<a id="s4-1"></a>
### §4.1 Findings from contributor registries with no term-level link (182)

These findings sit on a registry that contributes terms to this cluster, but their text and anchor verses don't resolve to any specific cluster term. Candidates for term-level enrichment.

| Finding ID | Type | Registry | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-6-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R006 anointing |  | Registry 6 (anointing) spans 7 dimensions across 38 groups — the widest dimensional range in C16. Session B should examine whether this breadth coheres around a unifying theme (Spirit-mediated transformation and divine endowment) or represents genuinely distinct inner-being phenomena requiring separate analytical threads. |
| DIM-6-002 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R006 anointing |  | Multiple Transformation groups in Reg 6 have GOD as dominant subject (167-001, 179-002, 4697-001, 4701-001, 4701-002). Session B should explore the full theology of God-initiated inner transformation in the anointing vocabulary — spanning Spirit-impartation, forgiveness, restoration, eschatological renewal, and judicial dulling/hardening as distinct expressions of the same divine transforming agency. |

| DIM-117-002 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R117 peace |  | The peace registry's inner-being content is unusually wide — spanning the felt inner state of rest/peace (Emotion — Positive), the inner posture of quietness before God (Moral Character/Relational Disposition), the divine giving of rest (Transformation/GOD), and God's own inner states of rest, restraint, and jealousy. Session B should examine what shalom names as an inner-being reality: is it primarily a felt state, a relational condition, a divine gift, or an eschatological reality — and how do these dimensions interrelate? |

| OBS-117-T2-001 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Judg 6:24, Isa 54:10, Num 6:26 | The peace registry reveals that shalom is constitutive of God's identity, not merely a condition he produces. Three data points establish this: (1) YHWH-Shalom (Judg 6:24, OBS-117-148) — the altar name declares God IS peace, not that God has or gives peace; (2) H7965G group 2508-002 (Isa 54:10, OBS-117-145) — "my covenant of peace shall not be removed" — the eternality of the peace-covenant is grounded in God's own unchangeability; (3) DIM-117-001 (OBS-117-019): LORD of Hosts appears throughout the corpus, establishing that the God of peace is simultaneously the God of eschatological power — peace is not weakness but the sovereign rest of the one whose power is uncontested. The theological anchor terms (H3073 YHWH-Shalom, H3071 YHWH-Nissi, H3072 YHWH-Tsidkenu) further confirm: God names himself by his characteristic acts and identities, and peace is one of those constitutive names. |
| OBS-117-T2-002 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Judg 6:24, Num 6:26, Psa 4:8, Isa 26:3, Jer 29:11 | Yes — extensively. God possesses shalom as identity (YHWH-Shalom, OBS-117-148, OBS-117-001), gives shalom covenantally (Num 6:26, Isa 54:10, OBS-117-145), makes shalom in his high heaven (Job 25:2, prior session OBS-117-103), plans shalom for his people (Jer 29:11, OBS-117-149), and speaks peace to his saints (Psa 85:8, OBS-117-145). The significance for the human person: because shalom is grounded in God's own identity, the human inner condition of peace is not self-generated but participatory — the human person receives and inhabits a peace that belongs to God. Psa 4:8 ("for you alone, O Lord, make me dwell in safety") is the clearest statement: the shalom of the inner life depends entirely on God as its ground. Isa 26:3 (OBS-117-144) confirms: perfect peace for the mind stayed on God — the directionality is always from God-as-peace-source to human-as-peace-recipient. |
| OBS-117-T2-003 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Mal 2:6, Psa 4:8, Lam 3:17, Jer 29:11 | Peace serves as the integrative condition of the human person's existence — the state in which the person is whole, functional, and in right relation with God, self, and others. The evidence from OBS-117-144, OBS-117-149, OBS-117-156 establishes this: shalom as wholeness of person (Isa 26:3 — mind, trust, peace as an integrated state), welfare of the whole person (Jer 29:11 — future, hope), soul's rest (Psa 4:8). The purpose is not merely psychological comfort but existential integrity — peace is the condition in which the person fulfils their creaturely purpose of walking with God (Mal 2:6, OBS-117-146: walked with me in peace and uprightness). Lam 3:17 ("my soul is bereft of peace; I have forgotten what happiness is") shows by negation: without shalom, the soul loses access to its own flourishing. |
| OBS-117-T2-004 | OBSERVATION | R117 peace | Psa 85:10, Isa 9:6, Isa 53:5 | The evidence shows both. (1) Peace as part of original design: Psa 85:10 ("righteousness and peace kiss each other") presents the eschatological restoration as a reunion of characteristics that belong together — implying they were originally united. The messianic reign of peace (Isa 9:6-7, Mic 5:5, OBS-117-147) is framed as the restoration of what was intended, not the creation of something novel. (2) Peace as response to the fallen condition: the "covenant of peace" structure (Num 25:12, Isa 54:10, Eze 34:25/37:26, OBS-117-145) presupposes a broken relationship being restored — covenant peace is given because natural peace has been ruptured. Isa 53:5 ("the chastisement that brought us peace, and with his wounds we are healed") explicitly frames peace as purchased healing of a rupture. Gap: the evidence does not directly address the pre-fall condition — Scripture's earliest peace statements (Gen 28:21, Gen 37:4) already presuppose the fallen world. The precise relationship between created peace and covenant-restored peace requires Session D synthesis with other registries. |
| OBS-117-T2-005 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 9:6-7, Isa 54:10, Jer 29:11, Psa 72:7 | Yes — and more strongly than almost any other registry. The eschatological orientation of peace is the most developed in the programme's data. Evidence: (1) H7965G group 2508-004 (DHC) — messianic peace is inherently future-oriented: "Prince of Peace" (Isa 9:6), "of his government and of peace there will be no end" (Isa 9:7), eschatological community dwelling in peaceful habitation (Isa 32:18), OBS-117-147; (2) H7965G group 2508-002 — the eternal covenant of peace (Isa 54:10, Eze 37:26) is a future-facing promise given in the present; (3) Psa 72:7 (peace abounding till the moon be no more), Isa 66:12 (peace extended like a river); (4) Jer 29:11 (plans for welfare, future, and hope — OBS-117-149) — God's peace-intention is explicitly teleological: "a future and a hope." Peace is not only what a person presently is but what they are moving toward. |
| OBS-117-T2-006 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Psa 120:7, Isa 26:3, Jer 29:7, Mal 2:6 | Peace expresses the divine image in two ways: (1) Relational shalom — the human person's orientation toward peace with others (H7965G 2508-003: "I am for peace," Psa 120:7; Mal 2:6: walked in peace and uprightness; OBS-117-146) mirrors God's own relational orientation of peace toward his people (2508-002, OBS-117-145). The peacemaker (H7965J 2510-001 — seeking the sha.lom of others) images the God who plans sha.lom for his people (Jer 29:7/11). (2) Inner peace as the God-oriented condition — Isa 26:3 (OBS-117-144) establishes that perfect peace is the condition of the mind directed toward God. This is not a neutral human achievement but an image-bearing posture: the human person who is oriented toward God-as-peace bears that peace as an inner condition. The divine image expressed through peace is the capacity for integrative wholeness — body, soul, relationships, and God all in right order. |
| OBS-117-T2-007 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Judg 6:24, Isa 26:3, Mic 5:5, Isa 54:10 | Shared — and with the unique feature that the sharing is constitutive rather than merely analogical. The evidence distinguishes: (1) God IS peace (YHWH-Shalom, 406-001, OBS-117-148) — divine ontological possession; (2) the human person receives peace from God and inhabits it (2508-001, OBS-117-144: soul bereft of peace; perfect peace for the trusting mind, Isa 26:3); (3) the messianic king IS peace (2508-004, Mic 5:5, OBS-117-147) — in the DHC structure, the divine-human boundary is breached in the direction of identification, not analogy. The peace that the human receives is not an analogue of divine peace but a participation in it — received from the same source (God), grounded in the same reality (covenant), moving toward the same telos (eschatological wholeness). This is a stronger connection than analogy; it is participation. The peace the human person bears is genuinely the same peace that God IS, received through covenant. |
| OBS-117-T2-008 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Psa 119:165, Mal 2:6, Deu 29:19, Isa 48:22, Psa 38:3 | The data provides clear evidence in both directions. Presence: the person who has shalom is in right orientation toward God (Isa 26:3 — mind stayed on God = perfect peace; Psa 119:165 — love of God's law = great peace; OBS-117-144). Mal 2:6 (OBS-117-146) — walking in peace and uprightness — is the portrait of the image-bearing priest. Absence: the absence of shalom is diagnostic of inner disorder. Three patterns emerge: (1) Moral disorder → absence of peace: Isa 48:22/57:21 ("there is no peace for the wicked"); the way of peace unknown to those in moral disorder (Isa 59:8); (2) False peace as image corruption: Deu 29:19 (2509-002, OBS-117-150) — the stubborn-hearted person who claims shalom without covenant ground; Jer 6:14/8:11 — prophets crying "peace, peace" when there is no peace; the corrupted image produces false shalom claims; (3) Somatic evidence: Psa 38:3 ("no health in my bones because of my sin") — the absence of shalom-wholeness has bodily expression. The image-bearing conclusion: shalom's presence is the marker of the person in right order with God; its absence (or false claim) reveals image-corruption at the deepest level. |
| OBS-117-T2-009 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Judg 6:24, Isa 9:6, Isa 53:5, Mic 5:5 | Yes — more explicitly than most characteristics in the programme. The typological structure is built into the vocabulary itself: YHWH-Shalom (Judg 6:24, 406-001) → Prince of Peace (Isa 9:6, 2508-004) → He shall be their peace (Mic 5:5, 2508-004) → He himself is our peace (Eph 2:14, G1515 group 426-003). Each stage names the same "X IS peace" ontological structure at a different historical moment. Isa 53:5 ("the chastisement that brought us peace... with his wounds we are healed") is the most compressed typological moment: the Servant's suffering produces peace as its direct result — and the NT reader recognises this as the mechanism of the peace Christ IS. The typology is not imposed on the text but inhabits it — the peace vocabulary itself carries the forward-pointing structure. DIM-117-SD003 (raised in DimReview session) targets this exactly. |
| OBS-117-T2-010 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Eph 2:14, Rom 5:1, Phili 4:7, Gal 5:22, Col 1:20 | Yes — and structurally so. The OT vocabulary names peace as a condition to be given, a covenant to be kept, a king to come. The NT vocabulary names peace as a person present: G1515 group 426-003 (Eph 2:14 — "he himself is our peace," OBS-117-122 from prior session). The Greek eirēnē carries all the semantic range of shalom (established by the LXX translation pattern) and then names Christ as the one in whom all those dimensions converge. The NT fullness: (1) Peace with God (Rom 5:1) — the relational condition; (2) Peace of God guarding hearts and minds (Phili 4:7) — the inner condition; (3) Christ IS peace (Eph 2:14) — the person; (4) Spirit-fruit peace (Gal 5:22) — the gift; (5) cosmic peace-making through the blood of the cross (Col 1:20, G1517 group 430-001) — the mechanism. The OT's four shalom dimensions (felt state, relational condition, divine gift, eschatological reality) are not rejected in the NT but fulfilled in a single person. |
| OBS-117-T2-011 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Judg 6:24, Eph 2:14 | The fulfilment of peace in Christ reveals that the original design was for the human person to live in the peace of God — not a condition achieved by the person but a Person known. The "YHWH-Shalom" altar name (406-001) names God as peace in the context of a theophany — the human person encountering God, receiving peace, and naming God as its source and substance. The fulfilment in Christ (Eph 2:14 — he himself is our peace) reveals that this was always the design: peace is not an abstract inner state but a relational reality grounded in the presence of the one who IS peace. The original design for the human person was to dwell in God's peace through covenant fellowship — and the NT peace in Christ is the restoration and fulfilment of that original design. The "dividing wall of hostility" broken down (Eph 2:14) is not a new problem solved but an original rupture healed. |
| OBS-117-T2-012 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Judg 6:24, Isa 9:6, Isa 26:3, Psa 4:8 | The primary Hebrew name is shalom (sha.lom, H7965G and sub-forms) — the most semantically wide term in the OT inner-being vocabulary. Its breadth is encoded in the STEP gloss: completeness, soundness, welfare, peace, quiet, tranquillity, contentment, friendship, covenant peace, peace from war (OBS-117-009). The name itself reveals that peace is not a simple state but a structural condition of completeness — everything in its proper place. Secondary Hebrew names: nachat (na.chat — quietness/quietude, H5183A), shaqat (sha.qat — to quiet/be quiet, H8252), nuach (nu.ach — rest, H5117), menuchah (me.nu.chah — resting place, H4496H). The primary Greek name is eirēnē (G1515) — which in the LXX became the translation word for shalom, absorbing its full range. The sub-names (YHWH-Shalom: "LORD is peace"; Prince of Peace: sar shalom) reveal that peace is not merely a human condition but a divine identity: the name carries what the named one IS. |
| OBS-117-T2-013 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Phili 4:7, Rom 5:1, Eph 2:14 | Strong continuity. The LXX translates shalom with eirēnē throughout the Hebrew Bible, establishing the semantic correspondence as the foundational datum of the NT peace vocabulary. The NT eirēnē carries the full shalom range: (1) Inner felt state (Phili 4:7 — "the peace of God... will guard your hearts and your minds," corresponding to shalom 2508-001); (2) Covenantal gift (Rom 5:1 — "peace with God through our Lord Jesus Christ," corresponding to 2508-002); (3) Moral orientation (Eirēneuō, G1514 — "live peaceably with all," corresponding to 2508-003); (4) Messianic embodiment (Eph 2:14 — "he himself is our peace," corresponding to 2508-004). The correspondence is not merely semantic but structural — the NT's peace vocabulary is the OT's shalom vocabulary transposed into the key of Christ. No significant discontinuity; the NT deepens rather than revises. |
| OBS-117-T2-014 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Lam 3:17, Jer 29:11, Isa 26:3, Psa 4:8 | The core inner-being essence of shalom is integrative wholeness — the condition of the whole person (body, soul, mind, relationships, and orientation toward God) in which everything is in its proper place and functioning rightly. This is not a narrow emotional state but an existential condition. The data establishes this through convergence: (1) The etymology of shalom (completeness, soundness — OBS-117-009) names the absence of fragmentation or deficiency; (2) Lam 3:17 (OBS-117-144) — "my soul is bereft of peace; I have forgotten what happiness is" — shows that shalom-deprivation is total inner destitution, not merely sadness; (3) Jer 29:11 (OBS-117-149) — "welfare... future... hope" — the three outcomes of God's sha.lom-intention show peace as the condition that makes flourishing possible; (4) Isa 26:3 (OBS-117-144) — perfect peace for the mind stayed on God — shows that shalom is the integrative outcome of right orientation. The essence is best stated: peace is the condition of integrative wholeness in which the person is complete, secure, and in right relation — capable of their full creaturely purpose. |
| OBS-117-T2-015 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Mal 2:6, Psa 34:14, Eph 2:14, Rom 5:1 | All four, in structured combination: (1) State: shalom as the inner condition of the person (2508-001 — inner peace as felt experience; 2509-001 — welfare as existential condition); (2) Act: shalom as active orientation and pursuit (2508-003 — "I am for peace"; Psa 34:14 — "seek peace and pursue it"; G1514 eirēneuō — actively being at peace with others); (3) Quality: shalom as the stable character quality of the peaceable person (Mal 2:6 — walked in peace and uprightness; G1516 eirēnikos — peaceableness as quality of heavenly wisdom; G2272 — gentle and quiet spirit as character); (4) Relationship: shalom as the condition of the God-human relationship (2508-002 — covenant peace; G1517 — making peace through the blood of Christ; Rom 5:1 — peace with God). The evidence does not privilege any one of these over the others — they are structurally interdependent. The relational dimension (covenant) is the ground; the state dimension (felt condition) is the fruit; the quality dimension (character) is the formed expression; the act dimension (pursuit, peacemaking) is the volitional engagement. |
| OBS-117-T2-019 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Psa 119:165, Psa 4:8, Isa 9:7, Lam 3:17 | Yes — the data shows at least four levels: (1) Shalom shalom (Isa 26:3 — perfect/complete peace, OBS-117-144) — the doubled word signals the superlative form, the fullest inner peace available to the trust-directed mind; (2) Great peace (Psa 119:165 — "great peace have those who love your law," OBS-117-144) — abundant but not doubled; (3) Present peace — the ordinary condition of shalom available to the covenant person (Psa 4:8, Num 6:26); (4) Absent peace — the condition of the bereft soul (Lam 3:17, Jer 30:5, Eze 7:25). Additionally: eschatological peace (Isa 9:7 — "no end to his peace") represents a fullness beyond present experience. The data does not articulate a formal scale but the textual evidence implies progression from absent through ordinary through great to perfect. The doubled shalom (Isa 26:3) and the "no end" formulation (Isa 9:7) mark the extreme ends of the spectrum. |
| OBS-117-T2-021 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Psa 120:7, Jer 29:11, Isa 45:7, Jer 30:5, Deu 29:19 | The data provides explicit antonyms: (1) War (milchamah) — Psa 120:7 ("I am for peace, but when I speak, they are for war"); the most direct antonym in the moral-orientation register; (2) Evil (ra'ah) — Jer 29:11 ("plans for welfare and not for evil"); the antonym in the divine-intention register; (3) Calamity/disaster — Isa 45:7 ("I make well-being and create calamity"); the antonym in the creational register; (4) Terror/panic — Jer 30:5 ("a cry of panic, of terror, and no peace"); the experiential antonym; (5) Stubbornness/iniquity — Deu 29:19, Mal 2:6 ("turned many from iniquity"); moral disorder as peace's contrary; (6) Anguish — Eze 7:25 ("when anguish comes they will seek peace, but there shall be none"). The antonym profile confirms that peace is not a neutral absence of distress but a positive condition with multiple contraries — war (relational), evil (moral), calamity (existential), terror (experiential), stubbornness (dispositional). |
| OBS-117-T2-023 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Psa 4:8, Judg 6:23, Psa 35:27, 1Ch 12:17 | The immediate responses to shalom's presence documented in the data: (1) Rest and sleep — Psa 4:8 ("in peace I will both lie down and sleep"); shalom immediately enables the cessation of vigilance; (2) Absence of fear — Judg 6:23 ("Peace be to you. Do not fear") — OBS-117-144; the divine peace immediately displaces terror; (3) Gladness and praise — Psa 35:27 ("shout for joy and be glad... Great is the Lord, who delights in the welfare of his servant") — OBS-117-149; shalom's presence triggers praise; (4) Heart-joining — 1Ch 12:17 ("my heart will be joined to you") — OBS-117-151; shalom's presence in friendship produces heart-union; (5) Daniel's strengthening — Dan 10:19 ("peace be with you; be strong and of good courage") — the angelic peace immediately produces inner strength. The pattern: shalom's immediate effect is the displacement of its contraries (fear, vigilance, inner fragmentation) and the enabling of their alternatives (rest, praise, courage, heart-union). |
| OBS-117-T2-024 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | R117 peace | Lam 3:17, Deu 28:65, Eze 7:25, Job 3:26 | Documented immediate responses to shalom's absence: (1) Soul bereft — Lam 3:17 ("my soul is bereft of peace; I have forgotten what happiness is") — total inner destitution, loss of access to happiness itself; (2) Bones wasting — Psa 32:3 (prior session: "when I kept silent, my bones wasted away through my groaning all day long") — somatic deterioration; (3) Trembling heart — Deu 28:65 ("a trembling heart and failing eyes and a languishing soul") — the triple somatic-inner expression of peacelessness in judgment; (4) Anguish seeking — Eze 7:25 ("when anguish comes they will seek peace, but there shall be none"); (5) Job's triple negation — Job 3:26 ("I am not at ease, nor am I quiet... I have no rest, but trouble comes"). The withdrawal of shalom is experienced as total inner collapse — not discomfort but destitution. The soul's access to its own capacity for happiness is severed (Lam 3:17). |
| OBS-117-T2-025 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 28:12, Jer 6:16, Isa 30:15 | Yes — the refusal of peace pattern is one of the most analytically significant in the registry. The data shows peace offered and refused: (1) Isa 28:12 ("This is rest, give rest to the weary... but they would not hear") — rest/peace offered and refused by Israel; (2) Jer 6:16 ("stand by the roads, and look, and ask for the ancient paths, where the good way is; and walk in it, and find rest for your souls. But they said, 'We will not walk in it'") — rest explicitly located in the "ancient path" and refused; (3) Isa 30:15 ("In returning and rest you shall be saved; in quietness and in trust shall be your strength. But you were unwilling") — the most concentrated statement of peace refused. The inability to receive peace is not ignorance but refusal — the will actively declines the condition. This pattern is concentrated in the OT prophets and names a structural feature of the human condition: peace is available but resisted. |
| OBS-117-T2-026 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Psa 119:165, Isa 32:17, Mal 2:6, Jam 3:18, Isa 30:15 | The sustained effects of shalom documented in the data: (1) Stumble-proof stability — Psa 119:165 ("great peace have those who love your law; nothing can make them stumble") — sustained shalom produces inner stability resistant to external shocks; (2) Wisdom reception — Isa 32:17 ("the effect of righteousness will be peace, and the result of righteousness, quietness and trust forever") — sustained peace is the condition in which trust is formed and wisdom operates; (3) Turning many from iniquity — Mal 2:6 — Levi's sustained walk in peace produced transformative effects in others; (4) Righteousness harvest — Jam 3:18 ("a harvest of righteousness is sown in peace by those who make peace") — peace-orientation produces righteousness as its long-term fruit; (5) Strength — Isa 30:15 ("in quietness and in trust shall be your strength") — the sustained inner posture of quiet trust produces strength. The sustained profile: shalom is not only an experienced condition but a formative one — it produces stability, trust, strength, and the capacity to impact others. |
| OBS-117-T2-027 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | R117 peace | Psa 38:3, Deu 28:65, Jer 12:12 | Sustained absence of shalom produces progressive deterioration: (1) Somatic degradation — Psa 38:3 ("no soundness in my flesh... no health in my bones because of my sin") — sustained peacelessness shows in the body; (2) Exile and homelessness — Deu 28:65 ("you shall find no respite, and there shall be no resting place for the sole of your foot") — sustained peacelessness produces the ultimate displacement; (3) Universal desolation — Jer 12:12 ("no flesh has peace") — when shalom is withdrawn from a community, the deprivation becomes total; (4) The wicked's false prosperity — Job 21:9 ("their houses are safe from fear") reveals by contrast: the wicked have external safety but not genuine shalom — the sustained absence of authentic peace produces the counterfeit of complacent ease. The trajectory: inner → somatic → communal → eschatological. |
| OBS-117-T2-028 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Mal 2:6, Heb 12:11, Gal 5:22, 1Pe 3:4 | Yes — and this is theologically significant. The forming dimension: (1) Mal 2:6 — walking in peace as the character-across-time of the faithful priest; the formed person whose sustained walk is peaceful; (2) G1516 eirēnikos — peaceableness as the fruit of discipline (Heb 12:11 — "the peaceful fruit of righteousness to those who have been trained by it"); (3) Gal 5:22 — peace as Spirit-fruit — the Spirit forms peace as a characteristic quality in the believer over time; (4) G2272 hēsuchios — the gentle and quiet spirit (1Pe 3:4) as the "hidden person of the heart" — a formed inner quality precious to God. The evidence confirms: sustained shalom is not merely experienced but formed — it becomes a character quality, an inner orientation, and eventually the "hidden person" of the heart. The transformative dimension connects directly to T5 (formative and developmental). |
| OBS-117-T2-029 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Lam 3:17, Psa 4:8, Psa 119:165, Isa 26:3, Phili 4:7 | Yes — as established in Q&A-020. The data shows: absent (Lam 3:17 — soul bereft), present (Psa 4:8 — lying down in peace), great (Psa 119:165 — great peace for law-lovers), perfect (Isa 26:3 — shalom shalom for the trust-directed mind), eschatological-unlimited (Isa 9:7 — no end to his peace). The NT adds: "peace of God which surpasses all understanding" (Phili 4:7) — the eschatological peace exceeds cognitive categories entirely. |
| OBS-117-T2-030 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Psa 119:165, Isa 32:17, Psa 4:8, Isa 30:15 | The data reveals a causal structure governing the degree of shalom: (1) Orientation of the mind toward God (Isa 26:3 — "you keep him in perfect peace whose mind is stayed on you, because he trusts in you") — the directing of the mind toward God produces perfect peace; (2) Love of God's law (Psa 119:165 — "great peace have those who love your law") — orientation toward God's word produces great peace; (3) Righteous character (Isa 32:17 — "the effect of righteousness will be peace") — the degree of shalom follows from the degree of righteousness; (4) Trust (Psa 4:8, Isa 30:15) — trust is the inner act that enables peace's reception; (5) The absence of stubbornness/self-deception (Deu 29:19, Jer 23:17) — the factors that reduce shalom are the absence of trust and the presence of self-deception. The causal structure: covenant faithfulness → trust → orientation toward God → peace. Each factor contributes; disruption at any point reduces the degree of shalom available. |
| OBS-117-T2-031 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 9:7, Eph 2:14, Phili 4:7, Isa 54:10, Rev 8:1 (cited via G4602) | Yes — and the eschatological fullness is among the most extensively documented in the programme's data. | OBS-117-T2-032 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 54:10, Num 6:26, Isa 26:3, Psa 4:8, Isa 9:6, Mic 5:5, Eph 2:14 | The most important single finding from T1: peace (shalom/eirēnē) is not primarily an emotional state or an absence of conflict, but an integrative wholeness grounded in divine identity and structured through covenant. The evidence establishes four dimensions that are not alternatives but a sequence: (1) Covenantal ground: shalom exists because God covenants it — the covenant of peace (Isa 54:10) is the basis; (2) Relational gift: God gives shalom to those in covenant (Num 6:26), speaks it to his saints (Psa 85:8), plans it for his people (Jer 29:11); (3) Inner condition: the received shalom becomes the experienced condition of the whole person — perfect peace for the trust-directed mind (Isa 26:3), soul at rest (Psa 4:8), welfare of the body and soul (Psa 38:3, 55:18); (4) Eschatological telos: the peace given and experienced is not complete until it is embodied in a Person — the Prince of Peace (Isa 9:6), he who shall be their peace (Mic 5:5), he who himself is our peace (Eph 2:14). DIM-117-002 (the pending finding about the nature of shalom) is hereby resolved: shalom is all four dimensions simultaneously, as a structured and connected reality. The central analytical finding is the sequence: divine identity → covenant gift → inner condition → eschatological embodiment in a Person. [RESOLVING DIM-117-002] |

| OBS-117-T2-039 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Lam 3:17, Psa 55:18, Psa 62:5, Psa 131:2, Jer 6:16 | Soul-level location establishes peace as a fundamental condition of the whole inner person's experience — not a cognitive state (mind-level) or a moral quality (character-level) but the experiential condition of the nephesh as living, feeling, wanting creature. This last point is analytically significant: the soul is not passive in relation to peace but can be called to orientation. The soul-level location means peace is the deepest personal experiential reality — the condition in which the self-as-person rests or is bereft. |

| OBS-117-T2-042 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Phili 4:7, Rom 8:6 | Yes — explicitly and centrally. The primary mind-location: Isa 26:3 ("You keep him in perfect peace whose mind [yetser — formed thought/disposition] is stayed on you, because he trusts in you") — OBS-117-144. This is the most direct mind-peace statement in the corpus: perfect peace (shalom shalom) is the condition of the mind that is directed toward and stayed upon God. The yetser is the formed inclination or disposition of the mind — its sustained directedness. In the NT: Phili 4:7 — "the peace of God... will guard your hearts and your minds [noema — thoughts, understanding]" — the mind is jointly named as the territory peace guards alongside the heart; Rom 8:6 — "to set the mind [phronema] on the Spirit is life and peace" — the mind's orientation determines whether peace is present. The mind is the second major constitutional location of peace after the soul, and the most explicitly causal: directing the mind toward God produces peace; directing the mind elsewhere forfeits it. |
| OBS-117-T2-043 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Rom 8:6, Phili 4:7 | The mind-peace connection primarily engages the mind's directional function — the capacity of the mind to fix itself upon an object. Isa 26:3 (yetser) — the "stayed" or "fixed" mind: peace requires the mind to be anchored, not drifting. The mental act that produces peace is not thought-content (what the mind thinks about) but mental orientation (what the mind is stayed upon). Rom 8:6 (phronema — the mind's settled disposition/inclination) — the mind's habitual orientation toward the Spirit produces peace; toward the flesh produces death. Phili 4:7 (noema — the products of thought, understanding) — the mind's thoughts are what peace guards: peace stands sentinel over the mind's outputs. Three aspects: (1) Orientation (Isa 26:3) — where the mind is directed; (2) Disposition (Rom 8:6) — what the mind is habitually inclined toward; (3) Output (Phili 4:7) — the contents of thought that peace protects. The mind's peace is a total engagement — orientation, disposition, and output are all in view. |

| OBS-117-T2-046 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | R117 peace | Psa 32:3, Psa 38:3, Deu 28:65, Psa 4:8, Isa 53:5 | Yes — and this is one of the most extensive somatic evidence sets in the programme. | OBS-117-T2-047 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | R117 peace | Psa 38:3, Deu 28:65, Psa 4:8, Isa 53:5, Psa 32:3 | The body-part links serve multiple functions: (1) Indicative — the body's condition indicates the inner-being condition: Psa 38:3 (no soundness in flesh/no health in bones because of sin) — the body reads out the inner state of peacelessness; the body is a diagnostic display of the inner condition; (2) Emphatic — Deu 28:65 accumulates three somatic signals (trembling heart, failing eyes, languishing soul) to intensify the portrait of peacelessness in judgment; the body amplifies the inner condition; (3) Expressive — Psa 4:8 (lying down and sleeping) — the body enacts peace by doing what peace enables; sleep is the body's expression of inner security; (4) Mediating — Isa 53:5 ("with his wounds we are healed") — the Servant's body mediates peace to others; the physical wounds are the mechanism of the relational restoration. The most significant body-link is Psa 38:3: the explicit naming of shalom as soundness-of-bones under sin's influence establishes that inner peace and somatic integrity are structurally connected — not metaphorically but causally. |
| OBS-117-T2-048 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | R117 peace | Psa 38:3, Psa 32:3, Isa 53:5, Psa 4:8 | Both directions are evidenced, with the dominant direction being inner-state → body: (1) Inner → body (primary direction): Psa 38:3 — sin disrupts inner peace → no health in bones; Psa 32:3 — suppressed confession (inner withholding) → bones wasting; Deu 28:65 — peacelessness in judgment → trembling heart, failing eyes, languishing soul. The inner condition of un-peace expresses itself through somatic deterioration. (2) Body → inner: Isa 53:5 ("with his wounds we are healed") — the Servant's somatic wounds produce inner healing/peace for others; the body of the Servant becomes the mechanism of inner restoration for the many. This is the most theologically significant body→inner direction in the corpus — a body bearing suffering that produces inner peace in others. (3) Body expressing inner: Psa 4:8 — the body lying down and sleeping expresses an already-present inner peace; the body does not produce peace but enacts it. The primary causal direction is inner → body; the Isa 53:5 direction (body → inner) is the unique redemptive reversal. |
| OBS-117-T2-049 | SOMATIC_EVIDENCE | R117 peace | Psa 38:3, Isa 53:5 | The primary direction (inner → body) establishes peace as a genuinely somatic characteristic — its absence or presence registers in the body because the body is the outward expression of the inner state. This has two consequences: (1) Peace cannot be fully present in the inner person while the body is in somatic distress caused by inner disorder — the body is a truth-telling indicator of the inner condition (Psa 38:3, 32:3); a person who claims inner peace while their body deteriorates under the weight of unconfessed sin is in the false-shalom pattern; (2) The redemptive reversal (Isa 53:5 body → inner) is extraordinary precisely because it runs against the normal causal direction: normally inner disorder produces somatic deterioration; in the Servant's case, somatic suffering produces inner healing in others. The directionality finding deepens the T1 paradox (Q&A-023): peace comes through its opposite conditions not only experientially but physically. |
| OBS-117-T2-050 | OBSERVATION | R117 peace | Psa 38:3, Pro 3:2 | The evidence provides indirect but not conclusive evidence for a bodily deposit. What is present: (1) Psa 38:3 and 32:3 establish that sustained absence of peace (inner disorder) produces somatic deterioration — bones wasting, no soundness in flesh. This implies that sustained presence of peace should produce the inverse — somatic health and soundness; (2) Pro 3:2 ("length of days and years of life and peace they will add to you") — wisdom-and-peace produces length of life; shalom is associated with longevity as its somatic fruit; (3) Pro 3:17 ("all her paths are peace") — wisdom's characteristic product is peace as a sustained life-condition. The wisdom literature implies that sustained shalom has somatic extension effects (length of life). However: the data does not explicitly address constitutional deposit in the technical sense (DNA, generational transmission). The silence is methodological rather than substantive — the biblical vocabulary does not operate with the category of genetic or physiological deposit. Gap: the question of generational or developmental deposit for sustained peace is not addressable from this data. This finding feeds directly into T5.7. |
| OBS-117-T2-051 | OBSERVATION | R117 peace | Pro 3:2, Psa 38:3, 1Th 5:23 | Supporting: Pro 3:2 (peace associated with longer life — a life-outcome that implies somatic extension); the somatic-deterioration pattern under sustained peacelessness (Psa 38:3, 32:3, Deu 28:65) implies by negation that sustained peace protects somatic integrity. Contradicting: no verse explicitly claims that shalom leaves a genetic or physiological deposit. The closest is Isa 66:12 ("like a river... like an overflowing stream") — the image of peace as overflowing suggests abundance rather than deposit. Neutral: 1Th 5:23 (the God of peace sanctifying the whole person — spirit, soul, body) suggests peace's reach is total but does not specify deposit mechanisms. The evidence supports somatic consequence of peace (in both directions) but not constitutional deposit in the genetic/biological sense. Gap explicitly noted for T5.7. |
