| OBS-117-T2-147 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Isa 54:10, Isa 53:5 | Three dominant argument structures: (1) Conditional-causal (if X then peace): Isa 26:3 — "you keep him in perfect peace [because] his mind is stayed on you [because] he trusts in you" — trust → orientation → peace; (2) Covenantal-declarative (God declares peace as covenant commitment): Isa 54:10 — "my covenant of peace shall not be removed, says the Lord" — the declarative form grounds peace in divine word; (3) Paradox-resolution (peace through its opposite): Isa 53:5 — "upon him was the chastisement that brought us peace" — the logical structure is the suffering of one producing peace for others; the conclusion is not deducible from ordinary cause-effect reasoning but from the logic of vicarious atonement. The three argument structures correspond to the three major peace dimensions: personal (conditional-causal), covenantal (declarative), and redemptive (paradox-resolution). |
| OBS-117-T2-148 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Num 6:26, Psa 4:8, Isa 9:6, Eph 2:14, Judg 6:23 | Primary contextual settings: (1) Covenantal: the covenant-of-peace texts (Num 6:26, Isa 54:10, Eze 34:25/37:26) — peace is given and confirmed in covenantal ceremony and prophetic announcement; (2) Liturgical/worship: Psa 4:8, 62:5, 85:8, 119:165, 131:2 — the psalmic context is personal worship and prayer; peace is experienced and expressed in the devotional posture; (3) Prophetic warning/lament: Isa 28:12, 30:15, Jer 6:14, Lam 3:17 — the prophetic context of peace refused, false peace proclaimed, and the soul bereft; (4) Eschatological vision: Isa 9:6/7, 32:18, Mic 5:5, Eze 34:25 — messianic and eschatological peace in prophetic vision; (5) Epistolary/communal: Rom 5:1, Phili 4:7, Eph 2:14, 1Th 5:23 — NT peace in the context of the Christian community and Paul's pastoral letters; (6) Crisis/encounter: Judg 6:23, Dan 10:19 — peace given in moments of personal encounter with the divine. The richest contextual setting is prophetic (both warning and vision) — the prophets carry the fullest peace theology. |
| OBS-117-T2-149 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Eph 2:14 | Two verses serve as joint primary anchors across the corpus — one OT, one NT: (1) OT primary anchor: Isa 26:3 — "You keep him in perfect peace [shalom shalom] whose mind is stayed on you, because he trusts in you." This verse names: the divine agent (God as keeper), the condition (shalom shalom — the doubled superlative), the constitutional location (mind — the directed mind), and the ground (trust). It is the most complete single-verse statement of the inner-peace reality. (2) NT primary anchor: Eph 2:14 — "For he himself is our peace, who has made us both one and has broken down in his flesh the dividing wall of hostility." This verse names: the person of peace (Christ = peace — ontological identification), the accomplishment (made one), the mechanism (his flesh/cross), and the scope (between peoples). Together these two verses — one naming the experience (shalom shalom for the trust-directed mind, Isa 26:3) and one naming the person (Christ IS peace, Eph 2:14) — constitute the definitive biblical statement of what peace is. |
| OBS-117-T2-150 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Isa 26:3, Eph 2:14 | Isa 26:3 uniquely: the doubled shalom (shalom shalom) — no other verse uses this superlative form; the combination of cognitive direction (mind stayed on God), trust, and the doubled-shalom outcome in one verse is unique. It establishes that perfect peace is not a goal to be achieved independently but a condition God actively maintains ("you keep him") in the person whose mind is properly directed. The subject-object relationship is: God keeps; the person's mind is the instrument; trust is the ground; shalom shalom is the outcome. No other verse combines all four elements so economically. Eph 2:14 uniquely: the ontological identification of a person with peace (he himself IS our peace) — no other verse in any biblical corpus makes this claim. "He IS peace" (not "he gives peace" or "he makes peace" — though both also appear) is the unique claim. The dual primary anchors together cover the experiential and the ontological dimensions of peace — neither alone is sufficient. |
| OBS-117-T2-151 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Psa 4:8, Isa 26:3, Jer 29:11 | Two frameworks are most directly relevant: (1) Positive psychology / wellbeing science: the concept of eudaimonia (flourishing/wellbeing) in Aristotle's ethics, and its contemporary development in positive psychology (Seligman's PERMA model — Positive emotion, Engagement, Relationships, Meaning, Accomplishment), maps most closely onto the shalom vocabulary. Shalom as comprehensive welfare and flourishing overlaps substantially with eudaimonia — both name the condition of the whole person thriving rather than merely experiencing pleasure; (2) Attachment theory (psychology): the Bowlby/Ainsworth framework of secure attachment producing a "safe base" from which the person can operate with confidence — this maps directly onto the peace-trust relationship (Psa 4:8 — resting in God's sole keeping; Isa 26:3 — mind stayed on God produces perfect peace). Secure attachment to God as the constitutional basis of inner peace is the closest psychological equivalent to the biblical structure. Neither framework is identical to the biblical concept — both illuminate without capturing it fully. |
| OBS-117-T2-152 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Psa 4:8, Lam 3:17, Psa 131:2 | Attachment theory illuminates three specific findings: (1) Psa 4:8 ("for you alone, O Lord, make me dwell in safety" → "in peace I will lie down and sleep") — the attachment-theory framework clarifies why trust in God enables sleep: secure attachment to God functions as a safe base that quiets the hypervigilance response, enabling rest. The physiological mechanism (sympathetic nervous system calming under perceived safety) provides the human science support for what the verse describes functionally; (2) Lam 3:17 ("my soul is bereft of peace; I have forgotten what happiness is") — in attachment terms, the peaceless condition is an anxious or disorganised attachment state where the person is unable to draw on the safe-base relationship; (3) Psa 131:2 (the weaned child with its mother as the model of the quieted soul) — this is the most explicit attachment image in the registry: a post-weaning child at rest with the mother is precisely the secure-attachment posture of calm at rest rather than anxious demand. The image is anatomically precise in attachment terms. |
| OBS-117-T2-153 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R117 peace | Psa 4:8, Eph 2:14 | Two points of divergence: (1) The source of the safe base: attachment theory locates the secure base in a human relationship (initially primary caregiver); the biblical data locates the ultimate secure base in God alone (Psa 4:8 — "for you alone"). Human relationships are a channel of sha.lom (H7965J friendship, 2510-001) but not its ultimate source; the biblical framework cannot be reduced to relational psychology because the foundation is not another human but God. The person who rests in a human relationship alone (without God as ultimate ground) is in the false-peace pattern; (2) The ontological claim (Eph 2:14 — "he himself IS our peace"): no psychological framework contains the concept of a person being a psychological condition. Peace as a person is beyond the scope of any human science framework. This is the most fundamental divergence: biblical peace has a Person as its source and ultimately its substance; psychology addresses conditions and mechanisms but not persons-as-conditions. |
| OBS-117-T2-154 | OBSERVATION | R117 peace | Psa 38:3, Heb 12:11 | Two gaps surfaced by the human science comparison: (1) Physiological regulation: the verse evidence shows somatic consequences of peacelessness (bones wasting, failing eyes, languishing soul) but does not address the physiological mechanisms connecting inner peace to somatic health — neuroscience of the stress response (cortisol, autonomic nervous system) would complement the biblical somatic evidence but is outside the verse data; (2) Developmental trajectory: attachment theory describes how secure attachment in early childhood shapes the capacity for adult peace and trust — the biblical data addresses formed peace in adults (Heb 12:11 — "those who have been trained") but does not address childhood formation of peace-capacity. Both gaps are relevant for Session C prose and for a comprehensive understanding of shalom's human experience, but they cannot be grounded in the biblical evidence directly. |
| SYN-INTRA-117-001 | SYNTHESIS_INTRA_TIER | R117 peace |  | The T1 analysis establishes that shalom/eirēnē names a structured four-dimensional reality — not alternative descriptions of one thing but a connected sequence: (1) Covenantal ground (God's covenant of peace, Isa 54:10); (2) Divine gift received (Num 6:26, Joh 14:27); (3) Inner condition experienced (Isa 26:3, Psa 4:8, Lam 3:17); (4) Eschatological embodiment in a Person (Isa 9:6, Mic 5:5, Eph 2:14). These four dimensions are not parallel alternatives but a causal sequence — each presupposes the preceding: covenant is the ground of the gift; the gift is what produces the inner condition; the inner condition points toward its eschatological fullness. This resolves DIM-117-002. |
| SYN-INTRA-117-002 | SYNTHESIS_INTRA_TIER | R117 peace |  | T2 establishes that peace is constitutionally mobile across all three levels (spirit, soul/mind/heart, body) in three documented patterns: (1) Cascading loss — inner disorder produces somatic deterioration (Psa 32:3, 38:3, Deu 28:65); the body is the last to fail and the indicator of deep inner disorder; (2) Cascading gift — divine peace received at the spirit level moves through heart and mind (Phili 4:7) into somatic rest (Psa 4:8); (3) Redemptive reversal — the Servant's wounded body produces inner healing in others (Isa 53:5); the primary causal direction reversed. The constitutional scope is total: "your whole spirit and soul and body be kept blameless" (1Th 5:23) — peace's sanctifying reach encompasses every level. |
| SYN-INTRA-117-003 | SYNTHESIS_INTRA_TIER | R117 peace |  | T3 identifies conscience as peace's primary gateway faculty — the inner faculty whose state most directly determines whether genuine peace is constitutionally accessible. Three conscience-patterns: suppressed conscience destroys peace somatically (Psa 32:3 — bones wasting); exercised conscience restores peace through confession (Psa 32:5); bypassed conscience produces false peace (Deu 29:19). No other inner faculty has this bidirectional gateway function as clearly documented. The moral evaluation faculty (T3.8) confirms: authentic peace enables right moral judgment; false peace corrupts it. The practical implication: the route back from peacelessness is through conscience-exercise (confession, acknowledgment, remembering God's faithfulness), not through direct emotional management. |
| SYN-INTRA-117-004 | SYNTHESIS_INTRA_TIER | R117 peace |  | T4 establishes two key relational findings: (1) Peace's scope expands progressively — covenant-primary (to Israel, Num 6:26) → covenant-expansive (to nations in the prophets, Isa 57:19) → universally offered through Christ (Eph 2:14, Col 1:20) — with the only sustained exclusion being moral ("no peace for the wicked"). The covenantal boundaries are overcome in Christ; the moral boundary remains. (2) Peace is a site of cosmic contest: angelic mediation of peace is effective (Dan 10:19), elemental disruption of peace is real (Mar 4:39), and eschatological removal of peace is documented (Rev 6:4). Peace is not only a private inner condition but a publicly contested reality across the cosmic order. |
| SYN-INTRA-117-005 | SYNTHESIS_INTRA_TIER | R117 peace |  | T5 establishes peace's unique dual role in the sanctification arc: it is simultaneously the condition under which sanctification proceeds (1Th 5:23 — the God of peace sanctifies) and the fruit that sanctification produces (Gal 5:22 — Spirit-fruit; Heb 12:11 — peaceful fruit of righteousness through discipline). This dual role means: (1) The person who persistently refuses peace is simultaneously refusing the conditions for their own sanctification; (2) The progress of sanctification is measurable partly by the deepening and stabilising of inner peace. The suffering connection (T5.4) adds: peace is not only formed in comfort but produced through suffering (Isa 53:5, Heb 12:11, Isa 38:17) — suffering is peace's formative companion, not its enemy. |
| SYN-INTRA-117-006 | SYNTHESIS_INTRA_TIER | R117 peace |  | T6 establishes peace as a hub characteristic with three primary structural bonds: (1) Trust (R163) — causal precondition: trust → peace (Isa 26:3, Psa 4:8); (2) Covenant (R34) — constitutional ground: the SHA.L root shared at root level; the peace-covenant is grounded in the same completeness-root; (3) Reconciliation (R130) — constitutive mechanism: reconciliation constitutes relational peace (Col 1:20, Eph 2:14). The causal system is reinforcing: trust → peace → strength → more trust. The hub position is confirmed by 25 co-occurring registries (≥3 verses) and 59 shared anchor relationships across 43 registries — the widest cross-registry engagement in C17. |
| SYN-INTRA-117-007 | SYNTHESIS_INTRA_TIER | R117 peace |  | T7 establishes that the peace vocabulary is structurally complete — covering state, disposition, act, and person-type — with a single root (SHA.L = completeness-wholeness-settlement) generating all Hebrew peace vocabulary. The vocabulary arc culminates in two primary anchors that jointly constitute the definitive biblical statement: Isa 26:3 (perfect peace for the trust-directed mind — experiential) and Eph 2:14 (he himself IS our peace — ontological). The most fundamental divergence from human science (attachment theory being the closest framework): biblical peace has a Person as its substance; no psychological framework contains the concept of a person being a condition. The NT coinage of eirēnopoieō (G1517) names what no OT term could name — the unique once-for-all act of making peace through the cross. --- |
| SYN-INTER-117-001 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T1 names peace's essence as integrative wholeness; T2 confirms this is constitutionally comprehensive — the soul (T2.2), heart (T2.3), mind (T2.4), hidden person (T2.5), and body (T2.6) are all in scope. The essence and the constitutional address are co-extensive: the integrative wholeness of shalom is not located in one faculty but distributed across all constitutional levels simultaneously. The soul is the most explicitly named OT location (Lam 3:17); the heart is the most comprehensive (engaging all four heart functions); the mind is the most causally explicit (Isa 26:3 — direction of mind → perfect peace). Together: peace is not a faculty-specific characteristic but a whole-person condition whose essence (integrative wholeness) matches its constitutional scope (spirit-soul-heart-mind-body). |
| SYN-INTER-117-002 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T1 names peace as integrative wholeness; T3 specifies how each inner faculty is engaged. The convergence: peace is integrative precisely because it engages all faculties — perception (enabling divine hearing), cognition (right orientation), memory (recovering forgotten happiness), affect (holding feeling rightly), volition (the most constitutive engagement — peace is chosen and refused), agency (liberated by authentic peace), moral evaluation (right judgment), conscience (gateway faculty), conscientiousness (integrated response enabled), and relational capacity (co-constitutive with interiority). The faculty engagement pattern confirms: peace is integrative because it involves every inner capacity simultaneously. The faculty that can most destroy peace (suppressed conscience) and most enable it (exercised conscience) is not the most obviously prominent but the most structurally foundational. |
| SYN-INTER-117-003 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T1 names peace as integrative wholeness; T4 shows its relational structure is not incidental but constitutive. The peace-wholeness of T1 is not achievable in isolation — it is given by God (T4.1), oriented toward God (T4.2), extended toward others (T4.3), and contested cosmically (T4.6). The interiority (T1) and the relationality (T4) are co-constitutive (confirmed from T3.11.3): the person at peace is the person in right relation — with God, with others, and with themselves. T4's expanding scope (covenant → universal) maps onto T1's eschatological dimension (the peace that has no end, Isa 9:7): the scope expands toward the same fullness that the essence reaches toward. |
| SYN-INTER-117-004 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T1 establishes peace as a four-dimensional structured reality (covenant → gift → inner condition → eschatological embodiment); T5 shows how peace moves through that structure developmentally. The sequence structure of T1 maps onto the formative sequences of T5: the covenant ground (T1 dimension 1) is the origin (T2.9); the gift received (T1 dimension 2) is the divine-word mechanism (T5.3); the inner condition (T1 dimension 3) is formed through discipline, suffering, and Spirit (T5.4/5); the eschatological embodiment (T1 dimension 4) is what the present experience anticipates (T5.6). The suffering connection (T5.4) fulfils the T1 paradox finding (Q&A-023): peace comes through its opposite because the Servant's suffering is the mechanism of the gift's purchase. |
| SYN-INTER-117-005 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T1 establishes peace's central T1 finding (covenant → gift → condition → embodiment in Person); T6 confirms this structure through the causal and constitutive relationships found in the corpus. T6's trust → peace causal sequence (Q&A-148/149) maps onto T1's "covenant → gift → inner condition" — trust is the human act that enables reception of the divine gift. T6's reconciliation-constitutes-peace finding (Q&A-153) maps onto T1's eschatological dimension — the cross-accomplished peace (T1 dimension 4) is what reconciliation produces. The shared anchor network (59 relationships across 43 registries) confirms that T1's four dimensions are each structurally connected to multiple other registries — peace is not self-contained but embedded in the programme's full inner-being ecosystem. |
| SYN-INTER-117-006 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T1's central finding (peace as structured four-dimensional reality culminating in a Person who IS peace) is lexically grounded in T7's root analysis: SHA.L (completeness-wholeness-settlement) names the essence at the root level; the sub-forms (G/H/I/J/K/L) map onto T1's four dimensions; and the two primary anchor verses (Isa 26:3 and Eph 2:14) name the experiential and ontological dimensions respectively. The lexical arc (root → state → act → person-type → NT coinage) maps precisely onto T1's four-dimensional sequence: the root names the ground (completeness), the person-type terms name the formed character, and eirēnopoieō (G1517) names the unique act that accomplishes the eschatological dimension. Word and meaning are structurally aligned. |
| SYN-INTER-117-007 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T2 maps the constitutional territory; T3 maps the faculties engaged. The synthesis: every constitutional level (T2) corresponds to faculty engagement (T3) in the peace data. Soul-level (T2.2) ↔ Affect (T3.4) — the soul's peace is primarily affective (Lam 3:17, Psa 62:5); Heart-level (T2.3) ↔ Moral evaluation + Volition + Conscience (T3.8/6/9) — the heart engages the moral-volitional-conscience cluster; Mind-level (T2.4) ↔ Cognition (T3.2) — the mind's directed orientation; Body-level (T2.6) ↔ Agency (T3.7) — the body's actions express inner peace; Hidden-person (T2.5) ↔ Conscientiousness (T3.10) — the hidden person of the heart is the site of the most integrated response. The constitutional and faculty maps are not independent but interlocking descriptions of the same whole-person reality. |
| SYN-INTER-117-008 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T2 establishes the constitutional location of peace; T4 establishes the relational directions through which peace moves into and out of those locations. The human receives peace (T4.4) through the same constitutional locations — the receptive soul (Psa 131:2, T2.2) and the directed mind (Isa 26:3, T2.4) are the reception points. The relational and constitutional analyses converge: peace moves through relational channels (T4) into constitutional locations (T2). |
| SYN-INTER-117-009 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T2 maps where peace is located; T5 maps how it is formed there. The constitutional movement patterns (T2.10) are the spatial description of what T5 describes temporally: the cascading gift pattern (God → spirit → soul/mind → body) is the sequence by which peace is received and formed over time (T5.2) through the mechanisms of divine word, Spirit, and discipline (T5.3). |
| SYN-INTER-117-010 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T2's body evidence (Psa 38:3 — no sha.lom in bones because of sin) connects directly to T6's finding that reconciliation constitutes relational peace (Col 1:20, Eph 2:14) — the same sha.lom that is absent from bones when sin is present is the sha.lom that reconciliation restores. The SHA.L root (T6.4.2) names completeness — and Psa 38:3's use of sha.lom for somatic soundness is directly rooted in this: sha.lom IS somatic completeness, sha.lom IS relational completeness, sha.lom IS covenantal completeness — one root, all dimensions. The constitutional and structural analyses confirm the same root-level truth from different angles. |

| SYN-INTER-117-012 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T3 maps inner faculty engagement; T4 maps relational directions. | SYN-INTER-117-018 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER | R117 peace |  | T4's relational scope findings (peace given to Israel → expanding to nations → universal in Christ) are lexically grounded in T7's vocabulary arc. T6's root-level finding (SHA.L shared with R34 covenant, T6.4.2) is validated and grounded by T7's etymology (T7.1.1 — SHA.L root meaning completeness-wholeness-settlement; sha.lam = to pay in full). The root-level semantic bond between peace and covenant (T6) is not lexical coincidence but semantic identity: they share the same root because they name the same underlying reality from different angles — the covenant is the relational structure of completeness; shalom is the experiential condition of completeness. | DIM-187-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R187 strength | 1 Sam 15:22 | Group 7013-001 (a.yil, ram) carries a verse-level valuation in which obedience (H8085H sha.ma) and attentive listening (H7181 qashav) are declared greater than sacrifice — greater than the fat of rams (1 Sam 15:22). Neither term is an OWNER in Registry 187; their inner-being weight is present in the verse but unregistered in the programme. Session B for Registry 187 should explore: (1) what the comparative structure of 1 Sam 15:22 reveals about the hierarchy of inner-being orientations toward God — obedience and attentive listening as the higher register; (2) how this valuation relates to the strength/capacity cluster's broader understanding of inner-being agency before God; (3) the relationship between sha.ma and qashav as paired inner-being acts that together constitute the responsive orientation of the person toward God. |

| DIM-117-SD003 | MEDIUM |  | Group 2508-004 (H7965G sha.lom — messianic/eschatological peace) establishes that shalom in the Hebrew prophetic corpus is constitutively identified with the person of the messianic king: Prince of Peace (Isa 9:6), He shall be their peace (Mic 5:5), upon him was the chastisement that brought us peace (Isa 53:5). This is the OT ground of the NT claim that Christ IS peace (Eph 2:14, G1515 eirene — R117 group 426-003). Session D must examine whether the he-shall-be-their-peace structure (person = peace) in the Hebrew prophetic corpus is the direct semantic antecedent of he-himself-is-our-peace in the NT — and whether this constitutes a single unified concept across both testaments that R117 shalom and eirene groups together document. Cross-registry targets: NT eirene registries (R117 own Greek groups), R130 reconciliation (Col 1:20), messianic-identity material. |

| DIM-187-SD001 | HIGH |  | Programme-level registry validation gap identified during C20 Dimension Review (2026-04-08). Root cause: STEP Bible treats suffix variants of a root (e.g. H8085G vs H8085H for sha.ma) as sub-glosses rather than as independently linked related terms. The Session A extraction pipeline follows STEP's relational architecture and consequently does not surface sub-gloss variants as candidates for independent extraction. H8085H (sha.ma — to hear/obey) was not extracted; H7181 (qashav — to attend/listen) was extracted but STEP shows its related-word set as identical to H8085G, masking the sha.ma/qashav relationship. These are foundational inner-being terms — the hearing/obeying and attending/listening cluster is central to the biblical account of the inner person's orientation toward God. Session D must initiate a backward validation sweep: for every registered term, check whether its STEP sub-gloss variants were independently assessed for extraction eligibility. Priority: terms where the H/G/I suffix pattern produces distinct semantic content. This sweep should be scoped and executed before Session D synthesis conclusions are drawn on the hearing/obeying dimension. |
| DIM-187-SD002 | MEDIUM |  | The oikos/oikia family in Reg 187 generates groups across at least seven distinct inner-being dimensions (Moral Character, Transformation, Agency/Power, Relational Disposition, Volition, Divine-Human Correspondence, Vitality/Existence). The household vocabulary functions as a structural metaphor for the inner life rather than naming a single characteristic. Session D should assess whether the household/dwelling family constitutes a distinct metaphorical register in the biblical account of the inner person. |
| DIM-187-SD003 | MEDIUM |  | The AMTS root family (am.mits, am.tsah, o.mets in Reg 187) is closely cognate with the CHAZAQ family (Reg 33/C08) in the biblical courage formula chazaq ve-amats (be strong and courageous). The split of these two roots across C08 (courage, verb forms) and C20 (strength, adjective/noun forms) is analytically significant. Session D should synthesise the full courage formula by reading the C08 and C20 groups together, addressing the verb/adjective split within the same root complex. |
| DIM-187-SD004 | MEDIUM |  | The directionally-determined pattern appears with particular density in C20 strength vocabulary. The same Hebrew root generates groups in opposite registers — divine greatness and human pride (GADAL), strength as divine gift and strength as misplaced trust (OZ, KO.ACH, CHAYIL), sure-footedness and collapse (TSAV). This pattern, established as a structural principle across earlier clusters, is most concentrated in C20. Session D should assess whether the strength/power cluster adds a specific contribution to the directionally-determined principle beyond what C08 (virtue/vice) and C09 (pride/majesty) already established. |
| DIM-068-SD003 | MEDIUM |  | C20 power cluster dimension overlap: strength (187), power (196), authority (197), might (198), dominion (199) — all share all 3 grace dimensions (Relational Disposition 9 groups, Moral Character 1, Dependence/Creatureliness 1). 2Cor 12:9 makes the structural connection explicit: power made perfect in weakness, grace as its modality. Session D should examine whether grace consistently names the relational mode through which divine power reaches the creature precisely where human power fails, and whether Dependence/Creatureliness is the inner condition that opens the person to both grace and power. |
| DIM-111-SD001 | HIGH |  | Strength/power/authority/dominion registries (Reg 187/196/197/198/199) share all 4 of mercy dimensions. Structural question: is mercy the moral direction of power toward the vulnerable? Session D to examine whether power and mercy form a structural inner-being pair. |
| DIM-103-SD026 | MEDIUM | G0025 | C20 cluster (strength/might/authority/dominion — Regs 187/198/197/199) shares all 8 dimensions with love and co-occurs in 69-105 verses. This may be a registry-breadth effect, but the co-occurrence is genuine and large. Question: does the biblical vocabulary connect love and power structurally? Is love the form that power takes in the kingdom of God, and power the form that love takes in creation? The 1Cor 13 sequence — love as greater than gifts of power and knowledge — suggests love and power are in deliberate tension in the NT. |
| DIM-064-SD019 | MEDIUM | G0859 | 19 shared verses between forgiveness (064) and strength (187) is the second-highest cooccurrence signal in this registry's corpus. The forgiveness passages frequently invoke divine power, exaltation, and authority in the same context as forgiveness: Acts 5:31 ('God exalted him at his right hand as Leader and Savior to give repentance and forgiveness of sins'), Num 14:19 ('according to the greatness of your steadfast love'). Session D question: does the programme's strength/power cluster (C20) address the relationship between divine omnipotence and the capacity to forgive at the scale Scripture describes? Is there an inner-being statement about divine power embedded in the forgiveness corpus that the C20 synthesis should address? Confirmed by 19 shared verses (strongest unexpected cooccurrence signal in this registry). |

| 50 | 111-001 | H1878 | Term names the inner enrichment or richly-supplied condition of the soul that flows from right inner character — the soul of the diligent is richly supplied (Pro 13:4; ne.phesh + da.shen is the only instance in the cluster where prosperity vocabulary is applied directly to the ne.phesh); whoever brings blessing will be enriched (Pro 11:25); the one who trusts in the Lord will be enriched (Pro 28:25). Good news refreshes the bones (Pro 15:30 — da.shen applied to inner-physical renewal through received blessing). Character (diligence, generosity, trust) is the inner condition that produces material and inner enrichment as its fruit. Anchor: Pro 13:4. |  |

Rov does not name wealth in itself but names the weight of what accumulates in the inner-moral domain — and how the magnitude of divine faithfulness exceeds the magnitude of human failure. Anchor: Isa 63:7 (abundance of his steadfast love); Hos 9:7 (great iniquity and great hatred). |  |
| 552 | 3836-001 | H5727 | Term names the inner act of luxuriating in or delighting in received abundance — specifically delighting in God's goodness as the source. Neh 9:25: they ate, were filled, became fat, and delighted (a.dan) in your great goodness. This is the ordered face of abundance received with joy and conscious orientation toward the Giver. The same verse that documents the prosperity-apostasy pattern shows a.dan as the inner act that preceded the turning — delight in goodness, if not tethered to the Giver, becomes the ground of forgetting. In its ordered form a.dan names the legitimate inner enjoyment of divine provision. Anchor: Neh 9:25. |  |

| 3709 | 7581-001 | G4149 | Term names material riches as the choking and deceiving inner force — the deceitfulness (apatē) of riches competes with the word of God for the inner person's receptivity and produces fruitlessness (Mat 13:22; Mar 4:19; Luk 8:14); riches that have been unjustly accumulated rot and are moth-eaten (Jam 5:2); the person who has riches set their hope on something inherently uncertain (1Ti 6:17). The word apatē names the mechanism: riches present themselves as satisfying and securing but they are deceptive — they do not deliver what they promise, they choke rather than nourish, they decay rather than endure. | 3710 | 7581-002 | G4149 | Term names riches in their revaluation by a higher inner-being calculus — the wealth of generosity that flows from poverty and overflowing joy (2Cor 8:2); the reproach of Christ counted as greater wealth than the treasures of Egypt because Moses was looking to the reward (Heb 11:26). In both cases the person's inner vision — what they are looking toward, what they count as truly valuable — has reordered the wealth calculus. The ploutos of genuine generosity exceeds material ploutos; the ploutos of Christ's reproach exceeds the treasures of Egypt. Anchor: Heb 11:26. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-D — New VCG. M46-D revaluation face. |
| 3714 | 7582-001 | G4433 | Term names the voluntary poverty of Christ as the paradigmatic act of the wealth domain's inversion — though he was rich he became poor, so that through his poverty we might become rich (2Cor 8:9). This is the foundational Christological statement of M46-D: divine wealth voluntarily surrendered; voluntary impoverishment as the means of others' enrichment; the through-put of self-impoverishment for others' benefit. Every act of voluntary release in M46 participates in or reflects this movement. Anchor: 2Cor 8:9. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-D — New VCG. M46-D. Sole verse — sole VCG. |
| 3706 | 7583-001 | G4434 | Term names poverty as the inner posture of dependence and openness before God — the condition in which the person has nothing to offer and is therefore constitutively receptive to divine gift. The poor in spirit (Mat 5:3) are not people lacking in spirit but those who know they have no inner resource to bring; the kingdom belongs to them. The materially poor are the primary recipients of the gospel (Luk 4:18; 4:20) and the heirs of the kingdom (Luk 6:20; Jam 2:5). God has specifically chosen the ptōchos of this world to be rich in faith. Material poverty may be the condition that most naturally removes the inner buffer of self-sufficiency and creates openness. Anchor: Mat 5:3. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-D — New VCG. Primary M46-D poverty-as-kingdom-ground face. |
| 3707 | 7583-002 | G4434 | Term names the poor person as the moral test of the wealthy person's inner condition — the assembly that pays attention to the rich visitor and tells the poor man to stand reveals what is in the heart (Jam 2:2-3); the community that dishonors the poor while honoring the rich has made a moral judgment about persons based on material condition; the false concern of Judas for the poor (Joh 12:6) reveals that invoking the poor can itself be an inner act of concealment. How a person treats the ptōchos is the index of their inner moral condition. Anchor: Jam 2:2-3. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-B — New VCG. M46-B — poor as the mirror of the wealthy person's inner condition. |
| 3708 | 7583-003 | H1878,G4434 | Term names voluntary giving from poverty and the command to give to the poor as acts that produce genuine enrichment and kingdom treasure. The widow who gave all her living gave more than all the wealthy (Luk 21:3; Mar 12:43) — her gift was total and was evaluated by Jesus as greater. The commands to give to the poor (Luk 18:22; Mat 19:21) are the specific acts of release by which kingdom treasure is obtained. Zacchaeus giving half to the poor is the spontaneous inner-being response to encounter with Jesus (Luk 19:8). The giving to the poor is both the external act and the inner act of relinquishing the attachment that wealth creates. Anchor: Luk 21:3. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-D — New VCG. M46-D — giving to the poor as act of release producing kingdom treasure. |
| 3718 | 7584-001 | H6223,H6239 | Term names the inner condition of the wealthy person whose material abundance has produced specific distortions — wise in their own eyes (Pro 28:11); unable to sleep from the restlessness of abundance (Ecc 5:12); answering roughly those who petition (Pro 18:23); exercising structural dominion over the poor (Pro 22:7); full of violence (Mic 6:12); unwilling to give from their own abundance, taking instead from the poor (2Sa 12:4); ignoring the suffering neighbor while feasting daily (Luk 16:19-21); going to bed rich and waking to find wealth gone (Job 27:19). Wealth produces a specific inner posture toward others and toward the person's own condition. Anchor: Pro 28:11. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-B — New VCG. M46-B. |
| 3719 | 7584-002 | H6223 | Term names the rich person in the wisdom tradition's moral examination — the rich and poor stand equally before God who made them both (Pro 22:2); better is the poor person who walks in integrity than the rich person who is crooked in their ways (Pro 28:6); the rich man unwilling to give from his own flock reveals a specific inner moral failure (2Sa 12:4 — moral lesson context). The wisdom tradition consistently evaluates the a.shir not by their material condition but by their inner character — and regularly finds that integrity in poverty exceeds wealth in crookedness. Anchor: Pro 22:2. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-C — New VCG. M46-C. |
| 3720 | 7585-001 | H6238 | Term names the inner drive to become rich as the source of moral failure and self-deception — Ephraim declares 'I am rich; I have found wealth for myself; they cannot find iniquity in me' (Hos 12:8): the self-declaration of wealth as the ground of self-assessed innocence; corrupt shepherds thank God for their enrichment while exploiting the flock (Zec 11:5); hastening to be rich brings punishment (Pro 28:20); the wicked will not become rich (Job 15:29). The inner motivation to accumulate — when it is self-directed and operates through exploitation or self-deception — produces the inner-closure pattern of M46-A. Anchor: Hos 12:8. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-A — New VCG. M46-A. |
| 3721 | 7585-002 | H1952,H6238 | Term names enrichment as the fruit of diligence and divine blessing — the hand of the diligent makes rich (Pro 10:4); the blessing of the Lord makes rich, and he adds no sorrow with it (Pro 10:22); the Lord makes poor and makes rich, brings low and exalts (1Sa 2:7). Inner character (diligence) produces material enrichment; divine blessing produces material enrichment without the hidden cost that self-generated accumulation carries. The same verb names enrichment as earned through character and as given through divine sovereignty. Anchor: Pro 10:22. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-C — New VCG. M46-C. |
| 3722 | 7585-003 | H6238 | Term names the deliberate refusal of enrichment as an act of inner integrity and wisdom — Abram refuses to take a thread or sandal strap from the king of Sodom lest the king claim to have made him rich (Gen 14:23): the inner act of not-being-enriched to preserve the testimony of dependence on God alone; wisdom counsels do not toil to acquire wealth, be discerning enough to desist (Pro 23:4). The inner discipline of restraining the wealth-seeking drive is itself an inner-being act of ordering the inner life beyond material circumstance. Anchor: Gen 14:23. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-D — New VCG. M46-D. |
| 3716 | 7586-001 | H1952,H6239 | Term names material riches as the object of misplaced trust and the condition of insatiability — those who trust in their wealth and boast of the abundance of their riches (Psa 49:6); the man who trusted in the abundance of his riches rather than making God his refuge (Psa 52:7); whoever trusts in riches will fall (Pro 11:28); the eyes never satisfied with riches (Ecc 4:8); wealth present but the power to enjoy it absent (Ecc 6:2); riches kept to the owner's hurt and then lost (Ecc 5:13-14); Haman recounting the splendour of his riches to his household (Est 5:11). Material wealth presented as the inner security foundation and found to be unreliable, insatiable, and ultimately alienating. Anchor: Psa 52:7. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-B — New VCG. M46-B. |
| 3717 | 7586-002 | H8082,H1952,H6239 | Term names material riches as the gift and fruit of the ordered inner life — Wisdom carries riches in her left hand alongside long life in her right (Pro 3:16); riches and honor are with Wisdom, enduring wealth and righteousness (Pro 8:18); the reward of humility and fear of the Lord is riches and honor and life (Pro 22:4); wealth and riches are in the house of the righteous, paired with enduring righteousness (Psa 112:3). Solomon chose wisdom rather than riches and received riches as the unasked-for consequence (1Ki 3:11-13; 2Ch 1:11-12). Both riches and honor come from God who governs all (1Ch 29:12). Anchor: Pro 8:18. | WA-M46-patch-vcg-from-reading-v1-20260514: subgroup=M46-C — New VCG. M46-C. |

### §4.5 Cross-cluster orphan findings/pointers

Findings + SD pointers that mention M-cluster vocabulary but originate from registries that do NOT contribute terms to this cluster — see [wa-cluster-m46-finding-orphans-v1-…](../../../outputs/markdown/) for the full scan.
